<unchecked> <start> Never has the upright ness of musicians , their genuineness , been put to such a dangerous test . <end>

<unchecked> <start> Victor Hugo and Richard Wagner they imply one and the same truth , that in declining civilisations , wherever the arbitrating power falls into the hands of the masses , genuineness becomes superfluous , disadvantageous , and a drawback . <end>
<unchecked> <start> It is only the stage player that still awakens great enthusiasm . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Thus dawns the golden age for the stage player for him and all that is related to his species . <end>

<unchecked> <start> EPILOGUE Let us finally , in order to take breath , withdraw for a moment from the narrow world to which all questions concerning the worth of persons condemn the mind . <end>
<unchecked> <start> A philosopher requires to wash his hands after he has so long occupied himself with the case of Wagner . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I give my conception of the Modern . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Every age has in its quantum of energy , a quantum determining what virtues are permitted to it , what virtues are proscribed . <end>
<unchecked> <start> It has either the vir tues of ascending life , and then it resists to the utter most the virtues of descending life or it is itself an epoch of descending life , and then it requires the virtues of decline , then it hates all that justifies itself solely by plenitude , by superabundance of strength . <end>
<unchecked> <start> aesthetics is indissolubly bound up with these biological presuppositions : there is decadence aesthetics , and there is classical aesthetics , the beautiful in it self is a chimera , like all idealism . <end>
<unchecked> <start> In the narrower sphere of so called moral values there is no greater contrast than that of master morality and morality according to Christian valuation : the latter grown up on a thoroughly morbid soil the Gospels present to us precisely the same physiological types which the romances of dostoievsky depict master morality Roman , heathen , classical , Renaissance re tersely , as the symbolic language of well of ascending life , of the will to power as the principle of life . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Master morality affirms , just as instinctively as Christian morality denies God , the other world , self renunciation nothing but negation . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The former communicates to things out of its fullness it glorifies , it embellished , it rationalise the world , the latter im perishes , branches , and mars the value of things , it denies the world . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The world , a Christian term of insult . <end>
<unchecked> <start> These antithetical forms in the optics of values are both indispensable : they are modes of seeing which one does not reach with reasons and refutations . <end>
<unchecked> <start> One does not refute Christianity , one does not refute a disease of the eye . <end>
<unchecked> <start> To have combated pessimism as one combats a philosophy was the acme of learned idiocy . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The concepts true and untrue have not , as it seems to me , any meaning in optics . <end>
<unchecked> <start> That against which alone one has to defend one s self is the falsity , the instinctive duplicity , which will not be sen bible of these antitheses as antitheses : as was the case with Wagner , for example , who possessed no little masterless in such falsifies . <end>

<unchecked> <start> NIETZSCHE CONTRA WAGNER : THE BRIEF OF A PSYCHOLOGISTPREFACE The following chapters are all rather carefully select ed out of my older writings some of them go back to , they are perhaps simplified here and there , above all , they are shortened . <end>
<unchecked> <start> When read in succession , they will leave no doubt concerning either Richard Wagner or myself : we are antipodes . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Something further will also be understood : for example , that this is an essay for psychologists , but not for Germans . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I have my readers everywhere , in Vienna , in St . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Peters burg , in Copenhagen and Stockholm , in Paris , in New York I have not them in Europe s flatlands , Germany . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And I might perhaps also have a word to whisper in the ear of Messrs , the Italians , whom I love just as much as I . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Quousque tandem , crisp . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Triple alliance : with the Empire an intelligent people will never make aught but a mes alliance . <end>
<unchecked> <start> FRIEDRICH NIETZSCHE . <end>
<unchecked> <start> WHERE I ADMIRE I believe artists often do not know what they can do best : they are too conceited for that . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Their attention is directed to something prouder than those little plants give promise of , which know how to grow up in actual perfection , new , rare , and beauty ful , on their soil . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The final excellency of their own garden and vineyard is superficially estimated by them , and their love and their insight are not of equal quality . <end>
<unchecked> <start> There is a musician , who , more than any other , has the genius for finding the tones peru liar to suffering , oppressed , tortured souls , and even for giving speech to dumb misery . <end>
<unchecked> <start> No one equals him in the colours of the late autumn , the baby pathetic happiness of a last , alder last , enjoyment he knows a sound for those secretly haunted midnight of the soul when cause and effect seem to have gone out of joint and every instant something can originate out of nothing . <end>
<unchecked> <start> He draws his resources best of all out of the lowest depth of human happiness , and as it were out of its drained goblet , where the bitterest and most nauseous drops have at the end the good or the bad ended with the sweetest . <end>
<unchecked> <start> He knows that weary of the soul which can no longer leap or fly , yea , not even talk he has the shy glance of pain that is concealed , of understanding without comfort , of leave taking without confession yea , as the Orpheus of all secret misery , he is greater than anyone , and much has been added to art through him only , much which was hitherto inexpressible and even seemingly unworthy of art the cynical revolts , for example , of which only the greatest sufferers are capable , and likewise many quite small and microscopic matters belonging to the soul , as it were the scales of its amphibious nature , yes , he is the master of minutiae . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But he does not willi to be so ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> His character loves rather the large walls and the audacious wall pain ting . <end>
<unchecked> <start> He fails to observe that his spirit has a different taste and inclination antithetical optics , and likes best of all to sit quietly in the corners of broken down houses : concealed there , concealed from himself , he paints his proper master pieces , which are all very short , often only one measure in length , it is not till there that he becomes quite good , great , and perfect , perhaps there only . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Wagner is one who has suffered sorely that is his pre eminence over the other must cans . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I admire Wagner in everything in which he sets himself to music . <end>
<unchecked> <start> WHERE I MAKE OBJECTIONS That is not to say that I regard this music as healthy , and there least of all where it speaks of Wagner . <end>
<unchecked> <start> My objections to Wagner s music are physio logical objections : for what purpose is to be served by disguising the same under aesthetic formulae ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> aesthetics is certainly nothing but applied Physiology . <end>
<unchecked> <start> My matter of fact , my petit fait rai , is that I no longer breathe easily when once this music operates on me , that my foot immediately becomes angry at it and revolts : my foot has need of measure , dance , march even the young German Kaiser cannon march according to Wagner s Kaiser march , my foot desires first of all from music the raptures which lie in good walking , stepping , and dancing . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But does not my stomach also protest ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> my heart ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> my circulation ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> do not my bowels fret ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Do I not unawares become hoarse thereby . <end>
<unchecked> <start> In order to listen to Wagner I need pastilles Ge braudel . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And so I ask myself , what is it at all that my whole body specially wants from music ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> For there is no soul . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I believe it wants L s alleviation : as if all the animal functions were to be accelerated by light , bold , wanton , self assured rhythms as if iron , leaden life were to lose its heaviness by golden , tender , unctuous melodies . <end>
<unchecked> <start> My melancholy wants to take its repose in the hiding places of perfection : for that purpose I need music . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But Wagner makes people morbid . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Of what account is the theatre to me ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> The convulsions of its moral ecstasies in which the mob and who is not mob ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> has its satisfaction ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> The whole pantomime of the stage player ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> It is obvious that I am essentially constituted : I have , from the bottom of my soul , for the theatre this art of the masses par excellence that profound scorn which at present every artist has . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Success in the theatre a person thereby sinks in my estimation , till he is never again seen non success then I prick up my ears and begin to esteem . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But Wagner was the reverse besides the Wagner who had made the lonesome of all music , essentially a theatre man and stage player , perhaps the most enthusiastic that has existed , even as a musician . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And in passing , we would say that if it has been Wagner s theory , the drama is the end , music is always but the means , his praxis , on the contrary , from the beginning to the close , has been , the attitude is the end , the drama , as well as music , is always only the mea . <end>
<unchecked> <start> ns . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Music as a means for elucidating , strengthening , and internalizing the dramatic pantomime and stage player concreteness and the Wagnerian drama only an occasion for many interesting attitudes ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> He possessed , along with all the other instincts , the commanding instincts of a great stage player in all and everything : and , as we have said , also as a musician . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I once made this clear , not without trouble , to a Wagnerian pur sang , clearness and wagnerian ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> I do not say a word more . <end>
<unchecked> <start> There was reason for adding further Be but a little more honest with yourself ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> for we are not in Bayreuth . <end>
<unchecked> <start> In Bayreuth people are only honest in the mass , as in individuals they lie , they deceive themselves . <end>
<unchecked> <start> They leave themselves at home when they go to Bayreuth , they renounce the right to their own tongue and choice , to their taste , even to their courage , as they have it and use it within their own four walls with respect to God and the world . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Nobody takes the most refined sentiments of his art into the theatre with him , least of all the artist who works for the theatre , solitude is wanting , the perfect does not tolerate witnesses . <end>
<unchecked> <start> In the theatre one becomes mob , herd , woman , Pharisee , the most personal conscience succumbs to the levelling charm of the great multitude , there the neighbour rules , there one becomes neighbour . <end>
<unchecked> <start> WAGNER AS A DANGERThe object which recent music pursues in what is at present called by a strong though obscure name infinite melody one can explain to one s self by going into the sea , gradually losing secure footing on the bottom , and finally submitting one s self to the element at discretion : one has to swim . <end>
<unchecked> <start> In older music , in an elegant , or solemn , or passionate to and fro , faster and slower , one had to do something quite different , namely , to dance . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The proportion necessary thereto , the ob service of definite balance in measures of time and intensity , extorted from the soul of the hearer a conti nous consideration , on the contrast between this cooler breeze , which originated from consideration , and the breath of enthusiasm warmed through , the charm of all good music rested . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Richard Wagner wanted another kind of movement he overthrew the physiological pre requisite of previous music . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Swimming , hovering no longer walking , dancing . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Perhaps the decisive word is thereby said . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Infinite melody just seeks to break up all symmetry of measure and intensity , at times it decides it even it has its wealth of invention precisely in what sounded to the ears of former times as rhythmical paradox and abuse . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Out of an imitation , out of a predominance of such a taste , there might arise such a danger to music that a greater could not even be imagined the complete degeneration of rhythmical feeling , chaos in place of rhythm . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The danger reaches its climax when such a music rests always more and more upon entirely naturalistic and pantomime , which , subject to no law of plastic art , desire effect and nothing more . <end>
<unchecked> <start> TheA MUSIC WITHOUT A FUTUREespressivo at any price , and music in the service , in the slavery of attitude that is the end . <end>
<unchecked> <start> What ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> would it really be the first virtue of a per france as the performing musical artists at present seem to believe , to attain under all circumstances a which cannon be surpassed ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Is not this , when applied , for example , to Mozart , the special sin against the spirit of Mozart , the gay , enthusiastic , tender , amorous spirit of Mozart , who , fortunately , was not German , and whose seriousness is a gracious , golden seriousness , and not that of a German Philistine . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Not to mention the seriousness of the marble statue . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But you think that all music is music of the marble statue , that all music must spring forth out of the wall and agitate the hearer to his very bowels . <end>
<unchecked> <start> It is only thus that music is said to operate ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Who is there operated upon ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Something on which a noble artist must never operate , the masses ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> the immature ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> the used up ! <end>

<unchecked> <start> A MUSIC WITHOUT A FUTURE Music , of all the arts that know how to grow up on the soil of a certain civilisation , makes its appearance last of the plants , perhaps because it is the most intrinsic , and consequently arrives latest in the autumn and withering of each civilisation . <end>
<unchecked> <start> It was only in the art of the Dutch masters that the soul of the Christian Middle Ages found its dying echo , their tone architecture is the posthumous , though genuine and equally legitimate sister of Gothic . <end>
<unchecked> <start> It was only in Handel s music that the best re echoed out of the soul of Luther and his kin : the heroic Jewish trait , which gave the Reformation a touch of greatness , the Old Testament become music , not the New Testa ment . <end>
<unchecked> <start> It was reserved for Mozart to pay in clinking gold pieces the balance due to the age of Louis XIV and the art of Racine and Claude lorraine it was only in Beethoven s and Rossini s music that the eighteenth century sang itself out , the century of enthusiasm , of broken ideals , and fugitive happiness . <end>
<unchecked> <start> All true , all original music is a swan s song . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Perhaps even our latest music , notwithstanding its predominance and ambition , has but a brief space of time before it for it originated out of a civilian in . <end>
<unchecked> <start> nose basis is rapidly i viv , a sunken civilisation . <end>
<unchecked> <start> A certain Catholicism of sentiment , and a delight in some ancient indigenous so called national existence , or nuisance , are its pre requisites . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Wagner s appropriation of old legends and songs in which learned prejudice had taught us to see something Germanic par excellence we laugh at that now , and the new inspiration of these Scandinavian monsters with a thirst for ecstatic sensuality and : all this taking and giving of Wagner in respect to materials , characters , passions , and nerves , would also express plainly the spirit of Wagner s music , provided that this itself , like all music , should not know how to speak unambiguously of itself : for music is a woman , We must not allow ourselves to be misled with regard to this state of affairs by the fact that for the moment we are living precisely in the reaction within the reaction . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The age of national wars , of ultramontane martyrdom , this whole interlude character which the circumstances of Europe at present are possessed of , may , in fact , assist such art as that of Wagner in obtaining a sudden glory , without thereby guaranteeing to it a future . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The Germans themselves have no future . <end>
<unchecked> <start> WE ANTIPODES It will be remembered perhaps , at least among my friends , that at the commencement I rushed upon this modern world with some errors and overestimates , and in any case as a hopeful person . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I understood who knows from what personal experiences ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> the philo optical pessimism of the nineteenth century as the symptom of a higher thinking power , of a more trim phil fullness of life than had found expression in the philosophy of Hume , Kant , and Hegel , I took tragical perception for the choicest luxury of our civilisation , as its most precious , most noble , most dangerous mode of squandering , but always , on the ground of its super abundance , as its permitted luxury . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I similarly inter pretend Wagner s music in my own way , as the express sion of a Dionysian of soul , I believed that I heard in it the earthquake with which a primitive force of life , suppressed for ages , finally relieves itself , indifferent as to whether all that at present calls itself civilisation is shaken thereby . <end>
<unchecked> <start> It is obvious what I misunderstood , it is obvious in like manner what I bestowed icon Wagner and Schopenhauer myself . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Every art , every philosophy may be regarded as a medicine and helping expedient of adv icing or decaying life : they always presuppose suffering and sufferers . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But there are two kinds of sufferers : on the one hand those suffering from the superabundance of life , who want a Dionysian art and similarly a tragic insight and prospect with regard to life , and on the other hand those suffering from the impoverish ment of life , who desire repose , stillness , smooth sea , or else ecstasy , convulsion , intoxication furnished by art and philosophy . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The revenge on life itself the most voluptuous kind of ecstasy for such improver wished ones ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> To the double requirement of the latter Wagner just like Schopenhauer corresponds they both deny life , they it they are thereby my antipodes . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The richest in fullness of life , the Dionysian God and man , may not only allow himself the spectacle of the frightful and the questionable , but even the frightful deed , and every luxury of destruction , de composition and denial , with him the evil , the sense less , and the loathsome appear as it were permitted , as they appear to be permitted in nature as a con sequence of the superabundance of the procreative , restorative powers which out of every desert is still able to create a luxuriant orchard . <end>
<unchecked> <start> On the other hand those suffering most , the poorest in life , would have most need of gentleness , and bene violence that which at present is called humanity in thinking as well as in practice : if possible , a God who is quite specially a God for the sick , a herland similarly also logic , the of existence as a conception , even for idiots the typical freethinkers , like the idealists , and beautiful souls , are all decadent in short , a certain warm , fear excluding narrowness and inclusion in opt mystic horizons which permit stupefaction . <end>
<unchecked> <start> In this manner I gradually learned to understand Epicurus , the antithesis of a Dionysian Greek in like manner the Christian , who , in fact , is only a species of Epicurean who , with the doctrine , belief makes blessed , carries out the principle of Hedonism as far as possible till he is beyond all intellectual righteousness . <end>
<unchecked> <start> If I have something in advance of all psychologists , it is that my insight is sharper for that nicest and most insidious species of inference a posterior in which most errors are made : the inference from the work to its originator , from the deed to the doer , from the ideal to him who needs it , from every mode of thinking and valuing to the ruling requirement behind it . <end>
<unchecked> <start> In respect to artists of every kind , I now make use of this main distinction : has the hatred of life , or the superabundance of life become creative here ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> In Goethe , for example , the superabundance became creative , in Flaubert the hatred : Flaubert , a new edition of Pascal , but as an artist with instinctive judgment at bottom : Flaubert est tumours , I lime n est risen , I oeuvre est tout . <end>
<unchecked> <start> He tortured himself when he composed , quite as Pascal tortured himself when he thought they both felt nepotistic . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Unselfishness the de cadence rmc Q , the will to the end in art as well as in morals . <end>
<unchecked> <start> WHERE WAG R Even at the present time France is still the seat of the most intellectual and refined civilisation of Europe , and the high school of taste : but one must know how to find this France of taste . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The Norddeutsche zeitung , for example , or he who has it for his mouthpiece , sees in the French , barbarians , as for me , I seek for the black part of earth , where theft h . <end>
<unchecked> <start> A AT slaves ought to be freed , in the neighbourhood of the Norddeutsche . <end>
<unchecked> <start> He who belongs to that France keeps himself well concealed : there may be a small number in whom it is embodied and lives , be sides perhaps men who do not stand upon the strongest legs , in part fatalistic , melancholy , sick , in part , over refined , such as have the ambition to be artificial but they have in their possession all the elevation and delicacy that is still left in the world . <end>
<unchecked> <start> In this France of intellect , which is also the France of pessimism , Schopenhauer is at present more at home than he ever has been in Germany his principal work twice translated already , the second time admit ably , so that I now prefer to read Schopenhauer in French he was an accident among Germans , as I am an accident the Germans have no fingers for us , they have no fingers at all , they have only claws . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Not to speak of Heinrich Heine I adorable Heine they say in Paris who has long ago passed over into the flesh and blood of the profounder and more soul breathing lyric poets of France . <end>
<unchecked> <start> What would German horned cattle know how to deal with the delicatessen of such a nature ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Finally , as regards Richard Wagner : one would seize it with hands , not perhaps with fists , that Paris is the proper soil for Wagner : the more French music shapes itself according to the needs of the dme moderne , the more it becomes Wagnerian , it already does so sufficiently . <end>
<unchecked> <start> One must not allowNIETZSCHE CONTRA WAGNERone s self to be misled here by Wagner himself it was sheer wickedness of Wagner to mock at Paris in its agony in . <end>

<unchecked> <start> The fact remains certain , nevertheless , for everyone who is acquainted with the movement of European civilisation , that French Romanticism and Richard Wagner are very closely connected . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Altogether dominated by literature up to their eyes and ears the first artists of Europe possessing a universal literary culture , mostly even themselves writers , poets , intermediaries and blenders of the senses and arts , altogether fanatics of expression , great dis covered in the domain of the sublime , also of the loathsome and the shocking , still greater discoverers in effect , in display , in the art of the shop window , altogether talented far beyond their geniuses , virtuosi through and through with dismal accesses to every thing which seduces , allure , forces , or upsets , born enemies of logic and the straight line , covetous of the foreign , the exotic , the monstrous , and all opiates of the senses and understanding . <end>
<unchecked> <start> On the w r hole , a rashly venturing , magnificently violent , high flying , and high up pulling kind of artists , who had first to teach to their century it is the century of the mass the conception of artist . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But sick . <end>
<unchecked> <start> WAGNER AS THE APOSTLE OF chastity this our mode ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> From German heart came this vexed undulating ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> From German body this self lacerating ? <end>

<unchecked> <start> Think well ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Ye still stay for impression , For what ye hear is Rome , Rome s faith without Chastity and sensuality are not necessarily anti chemical every true marriage , every genuine love affair is beyond any such antithesis . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But in those cases in which this antithesis really exists , it fortunately needs not at all to be a tragical antithesis . <end>
<unchecked> <start> This might at least be the case with all better constituted , more cheerful mortals , who are not at all disposed , without further ado , to reckon their fluctuating state of equip librium betwixt angel and petite bete among the arguments against existence , the finest , the brightest , such as Hafiz and Goethe , have even discerned an additional charm therein . <end>
<unchecked> <start> It is just such contradictions that allure to life . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But if , on the other hand , the ill constituted beasts of Circe can be induced to wor ship chastity , they will , as is but too plain , see and worship in it only their own antithesis and oh , one can imagine with how much tragic grunting and eager ness ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> that same painful and absolutely superfluous antithesis which Richard Wagner at the end of his days undoubtedly intended to set to music and pro duce on the stage . <end>
<unchecked> <start> For what purpose really f we may reasonably ask . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Here , to be sure , that other question cannon be avoided : what had Wagner really to do with that manly alas , so very unmanly rustic simplicity , the poor devil and country lad , Parsifal , whom , by such insidious means , he finally succeeded in making a Roman Catholic what ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> was this Parsifal really meant seriously f For that people have laughed over him I would least of all dispute , nor would Gottfried Keller do so . <end>
<unchecked> <start> One might wish that the Wagnerian Parsifal had been meant to be gay , like a finale or satiric drama , with which , precisely in a due and worthy manner , the tragedian Wagner had intended to take his farewell of us , also of himself , and above all of tragedy , namely , with an excess of the greatest and most wanton parody on the tragical itself , on all the awful earth earnestness and earth of the past , on the stupidest form of the of the ascetic ideal finally surmounted . <end>

<unchecked> <start> HOW I GOT FREE FROM wagner far back as the summer of , in the middle of the period of the first festival plays , my heart had taken farewell of Wagner . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I cannon stand anything ambit gurus and since Wagner s return to Germany , he had condescended step by step to everything that I despise even to Anti feminism . <end>
<unchecked> <start> It was , in fact , high time to take farewell then : soon enough I got proof of that . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Richard Wagner , apparently the most triumphal , while in truth become a decayed , despairing decadent , sank down suddenly , helpless and disjointed , before the Christian cross . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Was there no German then with eyes in his head , or sympathy in his conscience , for this awe inspiring spectacle ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Was I the only one who suffered from it ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Enough , to myself the unexpected event , like a flash of lightning , illuminated the position I had left , and also that subs quest horror which every one feels who has passed unconsciously through a fearful danger . <end>
<unchecked> <start> When I went further on alone , I shivered not long thereafter I was sick , more than sick , namely , fatigued : fatigued by the incessant deceiving concerning all that yet re gained for the inspiration of us modern men , concerning the strength , labour , hope , youth , and love squandered on all sides fatigued out of disgust for the whole ideal stick falsity and softening of conscience , which here once more had scored a victory over one of the bravest fatigued , finally , and not least , by the grief of an relent ing suspicion that I was henceforth condemned to mistrust more profoundly , to despise more profoundly , to be more profoundly alone , than ever before . <end>
<unchecked> <start> For I had had no one but Richard Wagner . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I was condemned perpetually to the Germans . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Lonely , henceforth , and sadly mistrustful of myself , I then , not without indignation , took sides against myself , and for everything which gave pain to , and was hard upon me I thus found the way again to that brave pessimism which is the antithesis of falsity , and also , as it would appear to me , the way to myself , to my task . <end>
<unchecked> <start> That concealed and imperious something for which for a long time we have had no name , until it finally proves itself to be our task , this tyrant in us retaliate frightfully for every attempt which we make to shirk it or escape from it , for every premature decision , for every thinking ourselves equal to those of whose number we are not , for every activity , however honourable it may be , if it happen to distract us from our main business nay even , for every virtue which might shield us from the sternness of our special responsibility . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Sickness is always the answer , when we are inclined to doubt con corning our right to our task , w r hen we begin to make it easier for ourselves in any respect . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Strange and frightful at the same time ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> It is our alleviation for which we must do the severest penance ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> And if we want afterwards to return to health , there is no choice for us : we must burden ourselves heavier than we were ever burdened before . <end>

<unchecked> <start> MORALITY AS ANTI NATURALNESSAll passions have a time when they are fatal only , when , with the weight of their folly , they drag their victim down and they have a later , very much later period , when they wed with spirit , when they are spiritualized . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Formerly , people waged war against passion itself , on account of the folly involved in it , they conspired for its annihilation , all old morality monsters are unanimous on this point : il fact ter les passions . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The most notable formula for that view stands in the New Testament , in the Sermon on the Mount , where , let us say in passing , things are not at all regarded from an elevated point of mew . <end>
<unchecked> <start> For example , it is there said with application to sexual it , if thine eye offend thee , pluck it out . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Fortunately no Christian acts according to this precept . <end>
<unchecked> <start> To annihilate passions and desires merely in order to obviate their folly and its unpleasant results appears to us at present simply as an acute form of folly . <end>
<unchecked> <start> We no longer admire the dentist who pulls out the teeth , that they may no longer cause pain . <end>
<unchecked> <start> It may be acknowledged , on the other hand , with some reason idleness that , on the soil out of which Christianity has grown , the notion of a of passion could not at all be conceived . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The primitive Church , as is well known , battled against the in intelligent in favour of the poor in spirit : how could we expect from it an intelligent var against passion ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> The Church fights against passion w T ith excision in every sense : its practice , its cure is castration . <end>
<unchecked> <start> It never asks , How to spiritualist , beautify , and defy a desire ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> it has , at all times , laid the emphasis of discipline upon extermination of sensuality , of pride , of ambition , of avarice , of revenge . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But to attack the passions at the root means to attack life itself at the root : the praxis of the Church is inimical to life . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The same means , castration , extirpation , is instinct lively chosen in the struggle with a desire by those who are too weak of will and too degenerate to be able to impose due moderation upon themselves those natures , which , to speak with a simile and without a simile , need la trapped , any definitive declaration of hostility , a gap between themselves and a passion . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The radical means are indispensable only to the de generate : weakness of will , or to speak more definitely , the incapability of not reacting in response to a stimulus , is itself merely another form of degeneration . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Radical hostility , deadly hostility against sensuality is always a critical symptom one is thereby justified in making conjectures with regard to the general condition of such an extremist . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Moreover , that hostility , that hatred , only reaches its height when such natures no longer possess sufficient strength for a radical cure , for labouring their devil . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Survey the whole history of priests and philosophers , that of artists also included and you will see : the most virulent attacks on the senses are not made by the impotent , nor by ascetics , but by impossible ascetics , those who would have required ascetic life . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The of sensuousness is called love it is a grand triumph over Christianity . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Our spiritual station of hostility is another triumph . <end>
<unchecked> <start> It consists in profoundly understanding the importance of having enemies : in short , in acting and reasoning the reverse of the former acting and reasoning . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The Church al ways wanted to exterminate its enemies : we , the immorality and Anti Christians , see our advantage in the existence of the Church . <end>
<unchecked> <start> In political matters also hostility has now become more spiritualized , much more prudent , much more critical , much more forbearing . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Almost every party conceives that it is advantageous for its self maintenance if the opposite party does not lose its power the same is true in grand politics . <end>
<unchecked> <start> A new creation especially , e . <end>
<unchecked> <start> g . <end>
<unchecked> <start> the new Empire , has more need of enemies than of friends : it is only in opposition that it feels itself indispensable , that it becomes indispensable . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Not otherwise do we comfort ourselves towards the inner enemy there also we have spiritualized hostility , there also we have understood its worth . <end>
<unchecked> <start> People are productive only at the cost of abounding in they only remain young provided the soul does not relax , does not long after peace . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Nothing has be come more alien to us than the desirability of former times , that of peace of soul , Christian desirability nothing makes us less envious than the moral cow and the plump of good conscience . <end>
<unchecked> <start> One has renounced grand life , when one has re bounced war . <end>
<unchecked> <start> In many cases , to be sure , peace of soul is merely a misunderstanding something different , which does not just know how to name itself more honestly . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Without circumlocution and prejudice let us take a few cases . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Peace of soul may , for example , be the mild radiation of a rich animality into the moral or religious domain . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Or the beginning of fatigue , the first shadow which the even ing every sort of evening casts . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Or a sign that the air is moist , that southern winds arrive . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Or un conscious gratitude for a good digestion occasionally called . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Or the quitting down of the convalescent to whom all things have a new taste and who is waiting in expectancy . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Or the condition which follows upon a full gratification of our ruling passion , the agreeable feeling of a rare satiety . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Or the senile weakness of our will , of our desires , of our vices . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Or laziness , persuaded by conceit to deck itself out in moral guise . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Or the attainment of a certainty , even a dreadful certainty , after long suspense and torture through uncertainty . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Or the expression of proficiency and mastery in doing , creating , effecting , and willing , tranquil breathing , attained freedom of will . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Twilight of the Idols : who knows ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> per has also just a modification of peace of soul . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I formulate a principle . <end>
<unchecked> <start> All naturalism in morality , i . <end>
<unchecked> <start> e . <end>
<unchecked> <start> all healthy morality , is ruled by an instinct of life , some command of life is fulfilled by adopting a certain canon of thou shalt and thou shalt not , some hindrance and inimical agency on the way of life is thereby removed . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Anti natural morality , on the other hand i . <end>
<unchecked> <start> e . <end>
<unchecked> <start> almost every morality which has hitherto been taught , reverence , and preached , directs itself straight against the instincts of life , it condemns those instincts , sometimes secretly , at other times loudly and insolently . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Saying that God looks on the heart , it negatives the lowest and the highest vital desiring , and takes God as the enemy of life . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The saint in whom God finds his highest satisfaction is the ideal castrate . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Life is at an end where the King dom of God begins . <end>
<unchecked> <start> If the wickedness of such a mutiny against life as has become almost sacrosanct in Christian morality has been understood , something else has , fortunately , been understood besides : the uselessness , the unreality , the absurdity , and the deceitfulness of such a mutiny . <end>
<unchecked> <start> For a condemnation of life on the part of a living being is ultimately just the symptom of a certain kind of life : the question whether rightly or wrongly is not at all raised thereby . <end>
<unchecked> <start> We would have to have a position outside of life , and yet have to know it as well as each and all who have lived it , to be authorised to touch on the problem of the worth of life at all : sufficient reason to convince us that for us the problem is inaccessible . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Speaking of values , we speak under the influence of the inspiration and the optics of life : life itself compels us to fix values life itself values through us , when we fix values . <end>
<unchecked> <start> It follows therefrom that even that anti naturalness in moral it which takes God as the counter principle and condemnation of life is but an evaluation of life , of which life ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> of which kind of life ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> But I have al ready given the answer : of declining , weakened , fatigued , condemned life . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Morality , as it has hitherto been under stood as it was his formulated by Schopenhauer as denial of will to life is the actual decadence in stint which makes out of itself an imperative : it says , Perish ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> it is the valuation of the condemned . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Let us consider in the last place what naivete it manifests to say , Man ought to be so and so ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Reality exhibits to us an enchanting wealth of types , the luxuriance of a prodigality of forms and trans formations and some paltry hod man of a moralist says with regard to it , to ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> man ought to be different ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> He even knows how man ought to be , this parasite and bigot : he paints himself on the wall and says , recce jomo . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But even if the moralist directs himself merely to the individual and says , You ought to be so and so , he still continues to make him self ridiculous . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The individual , in his antecedents and in his consequent , is a piece of fate , an additional law , an additional necessity for all that now takes place and will take place in the future . <end>
<unchecked> <start> To say to him , Alter thyself , is to require everything to alter itself , even backward also . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And in reality there have been consistent moralists they wanted man to be other wise , namely , virtuous they wanted him fashioned in their likeness , as a bigot : For that purpose they denied the world . <end>
<unchecked> <start> No insignificant madness ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> No modest form of presumption ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Morality , in as far as it condemns in itself , and not from regards , considerations , or purposes of life , is a specific error with which we must have no sympathy , it is a de generate idiosyncrasy which has caused an unutterable amount of harm ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> We others , we immorality , on the contrary , have opened our hearts for the recap tion , of every kind of intelligence , conception , and ap probation . <end>
<unchecked> <start> We do not readily deny , we glory in being affirmative . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Our eyes have always opened more and more for that economy which still uses and knows how to use for its advantage all that is rejected by the holy delirium of the priest , of the diseased reason of the priest for that economy in the law of life which even derives advantage from the offensive species of bigots , priests , and the virtuous , what advantage ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> But we immorality ourselves are the answer . <end>
<unchecked> <start> THE FOUR GREAT ERRORSError of confounding cause and effect . <end>
<unchecked> <start> There is no more dangerous error than confounding cone quince with cause : I call it the intrinsic depravity of reason . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Nevertheless , this error belongs to the most ancient and the most modern latitudes of the human race : it is consecrated even among us it bears the names , religion and morality . <end>
<unchecked> <start> It is con gained in every proposition which religion and morality formulate : priests , and legislators in morals , are the originators of this depravity of reason . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I take an example : everybody knows the book of the celebrated cornard , in which he recommends his spare diet as a recipe for a long and happy life , for a virtuous life also . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Few books have been read so much even yet many thousand copies of it are annually printed in England . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I believe hardly any book the Bible by right excepted has caused so much harm , has shortened so many lives , as this well meant curiosity . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The source of this mischief is in confounding consequence with cause . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The candid Italian saw in his diet the cause of his long life , while the pre requisite to long life , the extraordinary slowness of the metabolic pro cess , small consumption , was the cause of his spare diet . <end>
<unchecked> <start> He was not at liberty to eat little or much his frugality was not of free will he became sick when he ate more . <end>
<unchecked> <start> He who is not a carp , however , not only does well to eat properly , but is obliged to do so . <end>
<unchecked> <start> A scholar of our day , with his rapid con sumption of nerve force , would kill himself with the regime of cornard . <end>
<unchecked> <start> crude expert . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The most universal formula which lies at the basis of every religious and moral system is , Do so and so , refrain from so and so then you will be happy ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> In case of disobedience . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Every system of morality , every religion is this imperative I call it the great original sin of reason , immortal unreason . <end>
<unchecked> <start> In my mouth , that formula transforms into its inversion the first example of my Transvaluation of all Values : a man well constituted , a fortunate man , has to do certain actions , and instinctively avoids other actions he introduces the arrangement which he represents physiologically into his relations to men and things . <end>
<unchecked> <start> In a formula : his virtue is the result of his good fortune . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Long life and an abundant posterity are not the rewards of virtue : the very slowing of the metabolic process , w r which among other things , has in its train a long life , an abundant posterity , in short , Cornarism is rather virtue itself . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The Church and morality say that a family , a people , is ruined through vice and luxury . <end>
<unchecked> <start> My re established reason says that when a people is perishing , when it degenerates physiologically , vice and luxury follow therefrom i . <end>
<unchecked> <start> e . <end>
<unchecked> <start> the need of continually stronger and more frequent stimulants , such as every exhausted nature is acquainted with . <end>
<unchecked> <start> This young man becomes pale and withered at an early age . <end>
<unchecked> <start> His friends say that this or that sickness is the cause of it . <end>
<unchecked> <start> My opinion is that the fact of his becoming sick , the fact of his inability to withstand the sickness , was from the first the consequence of an impoverished life and hereditary exhaustion . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The newspaper readers say that this party ruins itself by such and such an error . <end>
<unchecked> <start> My higher politics say that a party which commits such errors is at its end its instincts are no longer to be relied upon . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Every error , whatever it may be , is the result of degeneration of instinct , disaggregation of will : we thereby almost define the bad . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Everything good is instinct and consequently , easy , necessary , free . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Trouble is an objection , the God is typically distinguished from the hero in my language : the light feet are the first attribute of Divinity . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Error of false causality . <end>
<unchecked> <start> It was always believed that we knew what a cause was but whence did we derive our knowledge , or , more exactly , our belief that we knew about the matter ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Out of the domain of the celebrated inner facts , none of which have hitherto proved themselves actual . <end>
<unchecked> <start> We believed that we ourselves acted causally in the exercise of will we thought there , at least , we had surprised causality in the very act . <end>
<unchecked> <start> In like manner people did not doubt that all the antecedents of an action , its causes , were to be sought in consciousness , and would be reds covered therein , if sought for as motives : for other wise man would not have been free to act , he would not have been answerable for his actions . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Finally , who would have disputed that a thought is caused ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> that the ego causes the thought ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Of those three inner facts by which causality appeared to be guaranteed , the first and most convincing is that of will as a cause the conception of consciousness spirit as cause , and later still that of the ego the subject as cause , are merely posthumous and have originated when causality , derived from will , was established as a given fact as empiricism . <end>
<unchecked> <start> In the meantime we have changed our mind . <end>
<unchecked> <start> We no longer believe a word of it all . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The inner world is full ot phantoms and will o the wisps : will is one of them . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Will no longer moves anything , consequently also it no longer explains anything , it merely accompanies proceedings , it can also be absent . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The so called motive another error . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Merely a surface phenomena on of consciousness , some accompaniment of an act , which conceals the antecedents of an act rather than manifests them . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And above all the ego ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> It has be come a fable , a fiction , a play upon words it has altogether ceased to think , to feel , and to will ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> What follows therefrom ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> There are no spiritual causes at all ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> The whole of the alleged empiricism that seemed to be in their favour has gone to the devil ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> That follows therefrom ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> And we had made a fine abuse of that empiricism : we had created the world on that basis , as a world of causes , as a world of will , as a world of spirit . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The oldest psychology and the longest maintained has here been at work , it has really done nothing else . <end>
<unchecked> <start> According to this psycho log , every occurence w r as an action , every action was the result of a will the w r world , according to it , be came a plurality of acting agents an acting agent a subject was insinuated into every occurrence . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Man has projected outside himself his three inner facts , that in which he believed firmest of all , will , spirit , and the ego , he only derived the conception of being from the conception of the ego , he posited things as existing according to his own likeness , according to his conception of the ego as cause . <end>
<unchecked> <start> What wonder that later on he always just reds covered in things what he had concealed in them ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> The thing itself , we repeat , the conception of a thing a reflection merely of the belief in the ego as a cause . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And even your atom , Messrs , the mechanisms and Physicists , how much error , how much rudimentary psychology , yet remains in your atom ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Not to speak of the thing in itself , the horrendous addendum of metaphysician ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> The error of spirit as a cause , confounded with reality ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> And made the measure of reality ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> And called God ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Error of imaginary causes . <end>
<unchecked> <start> To start from the dream . <end>
<unchecked> <start> For a definite sensation resulting , for example , from the distant shot of a cannon , there is a cause subsequently foisted on often quite a little romance in which the dreamer himself is the hero . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The sensation , in the meantime , persists as a sort of resonance it waits , as it were , until the causal impulse permits it to move into the foreground of consciousness now no longer as a fortuitous incident , but as meaning . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The cannon shot appears in a causal connection , with a seeming inversion of time . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The later , the motivation , is first realised , often with a hundred details which pass like lightning the shot follows . <end>
<unchecked> <start> What has happened ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> The ideas generated by a certain bodily state were mistaken for its cause . <end>
<unchecked> <start> As a matter of fact , we do just the same when we are awake . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Most of our general sensations every sort of check , pressure , tension , or explosion in the play and counter play of organs , especially the condition of the nervous sympathies excite our causal impulse we want a reason for feeling so and so , for feeling ill or well . <end>
<unchecked> <start> It never suffices us merely to establish the fact that we feel so and so : we only acknowledge this fact we only become conscious of it when we have furnished it with some kind of motif nation . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The recollection , which in such cases becomes active without our being aware of it , calls up earlier conditions of the same kind , and the causal inter relations associated with them , not their causality . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The belief that the associated ideas , the accompanying proceedings of consciousness , have been the causes , is also , to be sure , called up by recollection . <end>
<unchecked> <start> There thus originates an habituation to a fixed causal inter predation , which , in truth , checks the investigation of causes , and even excludes it . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Psychological explanation . <end>
<unchecked> <start> To trace back some thing unknown to something known , relieves , quiet , and satisfies , besides giving a sensation of power . <end>
<unchecked> <start> There is danger , disquiet , and solicitude associated with the unknown , the primary instinct aims at doing away with these painful conditions . <end>
<unchecked> <start> First pain simple : any explanation whatsoever is better than none . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Since , after all , it is only a question of wanting to get rid of depressing ideas , people are not specially care ful about the means for getting rid of them : the first conception , by which the unknown declares itself to be something known , is so pleasing that it is taken as true . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Proof of desire power as criterion of truth . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The causal impulse is thus conditioned and excited by the feeling of terror . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The why is intended , if possible , not so much for furnishing the cause on its own account , as for furnishing a species of cause a quitting , liberating , alleviating cause . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The first result of this need is that something already known , something experienced , something inscribed in the memory , is assigned as cause . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The new , the un experienced , the strange are excluded from being a cause . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Thus there is not only a mode of explanation sought for as cause , but a select and privileged mode of explanation that by means of which the feeling of the strange , the new , and the inexperienced , has been most quickly and most frequently got rid of , the most common explanations . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Result : a particular mode of assigning causes more and more , con centres itself into a system , and finally becomes predominant , i . <end>
<unchecked> <start> e . <end>
<unchecked> <start> simply excluding other causes and explanations . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The banker immediately thinks of busi ness , the Christian of sin , and the girl of her love . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The whole domain of morality and religion comes under this conception of imaginary causes . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Ex planation of unpleasant general feelings : They are determined by beings hostile to us evil spirits : the most striking case mistaking hysterics for witches . <end>
<unchecked> <start> They are determined by conduct not to be approved of the feeling of sin , of sinfulness , foisted on to a physiological unpleasantness one always finds rea sons for being discontented with one s self . <end>
<unchecked> <start> They are determined as punishments , as a recital for something we should not have done , for being otherwise than we ought to be audaciously generalised by Schopenhauer into a thesis in which morality appears undisguised , as the actual poisoner and of life : every sore pain , whether bodily or mental , indicates what we deserve , for it could not come upon us , unless we deserved it . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Welt als Wille und Vorstellung , They are determined as consequences of inconsiderate actions , which turn out badly the emotions , the senses , assigned as cause , as guilty states of physio logical trouble explained as deserved by means of other states of trouble . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Explanations of pleasant general feelings : They are determined by trust in God . <end>
<unchecked> <start> They are determined by the consciousness of good conduct so called good conscience , a why biological condition sometimes so like a g good di question as to be mistaken for it . <end>
<unchecked> <start> They are determined by the successful issue of undertakings a naive fallacy : the successful issue of an undertaking does not at all produce any pleasant general feelings in a hypo , or in a Pascal . <end>
<unchecked> <start> They are determined by faith , hope , and love the Christian virtues . <end>
<unchecked> <start> In fact , all these presumed explanations are resulting con editions , and as it were translations of pleasant and unpleasant feelings into a false dialect : we are in a condition to be hopeful , because our fundamental physiological feeling is again strong and rich we trust in God , because the feeling of fullness and of strength gives us peace . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Morality and religion be long entirely to the Psychology of Error : in every individual case cause and consequence are confounded or truth is confounded with the result of what is believed to be true or a condition of consciousness is confounded with the causation of this condition . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Error of free will . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Now we have no longer sum path with the notion of free will : we know only too well what it is the most disreputable of all theological devices for the purpose of making men responsible in their sense of the word , that is , for the purpose of making them dependent on theologians . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Here , I only give the psychology of the process of making men responsible . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Wherever responsibility is sought after , it is usually the instinct prompting to punish and condemn which seeks after it . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Becoming has been divested of its innocence when any mode of being whatsoever is traced back to will , to purposes , or acts of responsibility : the dogma of will has principally been invented for the purpose of punish ment , i . <end>
<unchecked> <start> e . <end>
<unchecked> <start> with the intention of finding guilty . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The whole of old psychology , will psychology , would have been impossible but for the fact that its origin actors the priests at the head of the old com wanted to create for themselves a right to impose punishment or a right for God to do so . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Men were imagined to be free , in order that they might be condemned and punished , in order that they might become guilty : consequently every activity had to be thought of as voluntary , the origin of every activity had to be thought of as residing in conscious ness whereby the most absolute false coinage in psychologies was made a principle of psychology it self . <end>
<unchecked> <start> now when we have entered upon a move ment in the opposite direction , when we immorality especially endeavour with all our power to remove out of the world the notions of guilt and punishment , and seek to cleanse psychology , history , nature , social institutions and sanctions from these notions , there is not in our eyes any more fundamental antagonism than that of theologians , who , with the notion of a moral order of the world , go on tainting the innocence of becoming with punishment and guilt . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Christianity is the hangman s metaphysics . <end>
<unchecked> <start> What alone can our teaching be ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> That no one gives a man his qualities , neither God , nor society , nor his parents and ancestors , nor he himself the latter absurd idea here put aside has been taught as intel bible freedom by Kant , perhaps also by Plato . <end>
<unchecked> <start> No one is responsible for existing at all , for being formed so and so , for being placed under those cir substances and in this environment . <end>
<unchecked> <start> His own destiny cannon be disentangled from the destiny of all else in past and future . <end>
<unchecked> <start> He is not the result of a special purpose , a will , or an aim , the attempt is not here made to reach an ideal of man , an ideal of happiness , or an ideal of morality it is absurd to try to shunt off man s nature towards some goal . <end>
<unchecked> <start> We have invented the notion of a goal : in reality a goal is lacking . <end>
<unchecked> <start> We are necks say , we are part of destiny , we belong to the whole , we exist in the whole , there is nothing which could judge , measure , compare , or condemn our being , for that would be to judge , measure , compare , and condemn the whole . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But there is nothing outside of the whole This only is the : that no one be made responsible any longer , that the mode of being be not traced back to a causa prima , that the world be not regarded as a unity , either as tentorium or as spirit it is only thereby that the innocence of becoming is again restored . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The concept of God has hitherto been the greatest objection to existence . <end>
<unchecked> <start> We deny God , we deny responsibility by denying God : it is only thereby that we save the world . <end>
<unchecked> <start> THE IMPROVERS OF mankind is known what I require of philosophers namely , to take up their position beyond good and evil , to be superior to the illusion of moral sentiment . <end>
<unchecked> <start> This requirement follows from a principle which I form later for the first time , namely , that there is no such thing as a moral fact . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Moral sentiment has this in common with religious sentiment : it believes in realities which do not exist . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Morality is only an interpretation of certain phenomena , or , more definitely , a interpretation of them . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Moral sentiment belongs , like religious sentiment , to a stage of ignorance in which the very notion of the real , the distinction between the real and the imaginary , is yet lacking : accordingly , at such a stage of intellectual develop ment , truth designates nothing but what we at present call fancies . <end>
<unchecked> <start> In so far the moral sentiment is never to be taken literally : as such it contains nothing but absurdity . <end>
<unchecked> <start> As semiotic , however , its worth remains inestimable : it reveals , at least to the initiated , the most important realities of civilisations and internal operations which did not know sufficient to under stand themselves . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Morality is merely sign language , merely symptomatology one has to know beforehand what it deals with , in order to derive advantage from it . <end>
<unchecked> <start> A first example , and quite preliminary . <end>
<unchecked> <start> At all times efforts have been made to improve human beings : it is that above all things which has been termed morality . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The most different tendencies , however , are concealed under the same name . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The taming of animal man , as w ell as the breeding of a particular species of human beings , has been called improving only these zoological termini express realities , realities , indeed , of which the typical improver , the priest , knows nothing does not want to know any thing . <end>
<unchecked> <start> To call the taming of an animal the improv ing of it , sounds almost like a joke to our ears . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Anybody who knows what goes on in menagerie will be doubtful about the improving of animals there . <end>
<unchecked> <start> They are weakened , they are made less mischievous , they become sick by the depressing emotion of fear , by pain , wounds , and hunger . <end>
<unchecked> <start> It is precisely the same with tamed man whom the priest has improved . <end>
<unchecked> <start> In the early Middle Ages , when in fact the Church was a menagerie more than anything else , the finest specimens of the blond beast were everywhere pursued the distinguished germanic for example were improved . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Afterwards , however , how did such a Germanic look when improved , when seduced into the monastery ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Like a caricature of man , like an ab option : he had become a sinner , he stuck fast in the cage , he had got shut up in the midst of no thing but frightful notions . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And now he lay there , sick , miserable , ill disposed towards himself full of hatred against the vital instincts , full of suspicion with regard to everything still strong and happy . <end>
<unchecked> <start> In short , a Christian . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Physiologically explained : in combat with the animal , the only means for making it weak can be to sicken it . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The Church understood this : it ruined man , it weakened him , but it claimed to have improved him . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Let us take the other case of so called morality , the case of breeding a distinct race and species . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Ind ian morality , sanctioned into a religion as the Law of Manu , furnishes the grandest example . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The task is here set to breed no fewer than four races all at once : a priestly race , a warrior race , a trading and ari cultural race , and , finally , a menial race , the sudan . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Here we are obviously no longer among the tamers of animals a race of men a hundred times milder and more reasonable is presupposed , even to conceive the plan of such a system of breeding . <end>
<unchecked> <start> One recovers breath on stepping into this healthier , higher , and wider world out of the sickroom air and prison air of Christianity . <end>
<unchecked> <start> How paltry is the New Testament in comparison with Manu , what a bad odour it has ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> But that organisation also required to be formidable , not , this time , in combat with the beast , but with its own antithesis , the non caste man , the mishmash man , the chantal . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And again it had no other ex pediment for making him harmless , for making him weak , except making him sick , it was the struggle with the great number . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Perhaps there is nothing more repugnant to our feelings than tawse preach binary measures of Indian morality . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The third edict for example adana astra I . <end>
<unchecked> <start> concerning unclean potherbs , ordain that the sole food allowed to the Chandalas shall be garlic and onions , considering that the holy writings forbid giving them grain , fruits , water and fire . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The same edict ordain that the water they require must neither be taken out of rivers , springs , or ponds , but only out of the entrances to swamps , and out of holes made by the footsteps of animals . <end>
<unchecked> <start> In the same manner they are forbidden both to wash their clothes and to wash themselves , since the water , which is conceded to them as a favour , must only be used to quench their thirst . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Finally , there is a prohibition forbidding the supra women to assist the chantal women at child birth , in like manner also a prohibition forbidding the latter to assist one another on such occasions . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The result of such sanitary regulations did not fail to appear : deadly epidemics , frightful sexual diseases , and , in consequence thereof , the law of the knife once more , which ordained circumcision for the male child ren and the removal of the labia minor a in the females . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Manu himself says : The Chandalas are the fruit of adultery , incest , and crime this is the necessary consequence of the concept of breeding . <end>
<unchecked> <start> They shall only have the rags of corpses for clothing , for vessels they shall only have broken pottery , for ornaments old iron , for the worship of God only the evil spirits they shall wander from place to place without repose . <end>
<unchecked> <start> They are forbidden to write from left to right , or to use the right hand in writing : the use of the right hand and from left to right are reserved exclusively for the vir tous , for persons of race These enactments are sufficiently instructive : here for once we have Aryan humanity , perfectly pure , per factly original , we learn that the idea of pure blood is the contrary of a harmless idea . <end>
<unchecked> <start> On the other hand , it becomes manifest in which nation the hatred , the chantal hatred against this humanity , has im formalised itself , where it has become religion , and genius . <end>
<unchecked> <start> From this point of view the Gospels are documents of the first importance , and the book of Enoch even more so . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Christianity springing out of a Jewish root , and only comprehensible as a growth of this soil , represents the movement counter to every morality of breeding , of race , and of privilege : it is anti Aryan religion par excellence : Christianity , the of all Aryan values , the triumph of chantal values , the gospel preached to the poor and lowly , the collective insurrection against race of all the down trodden , the wretched , the ill conti tuned , the misfortune , undying chantal revenge as religion of love . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The morality of breeding and the morality of taming are perfectly worthy of one another as regards the expedients for achieving their ends : we may lay it down as our highest proposition , that in order to create morality , it is necessary to have the absolute will to the contrary . <end>
<unchecked> <start> This is the great , the unearthly problem which I have longest applied myself to : the psychology of the improvers of mankind . <end>
<unchecked> <start> A small and modest matter after all , so called pia fraud , gave me the first access to this problem : fia fraud , the heritage of all philosophers and priests who have improved mankind . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Neither Manu , nor Plato , nor Confucius , nor the Jewish and Christian teachers , have ever doubted of their right to use falsehood . <end>
<unchecked> <start> They have not doubted with regard to quite other rights . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Expressed in a formula one might say that all the measures hitherto used for the purpose of moralising mankind , have been fundamentally immoral . <end>
<unchecked> <start> WHAT THE GERMANS LACKAmong Germans at present , it is not sufficient to have esprit one must appropriate it practically , one must presume to have it . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Perhaps I know the Germans , perhaps I may even say a few truths to them . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Modern Germany exhibits a great amount of hereditary and indoctrinated cap city , so that it can even spend prodigal for a while its accumulated treasure of force . <end>
<unchecked> <start> It is not a high civilisation that has here gained the ascendency , still less a delicate taste , or a superior beauty of the instincts , but earlier virtues than any other country in Europe can exhibit . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Much good humour and self-respect , much firmness in dealing with one another , in reciprocity of obligations , much , much endurance , and a hereditary moderation which re squires the goad rather than the brake . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I also add that here there is still obedience , without its being humiliating . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And nobody despises his opponent . <end>
<unchecked> <start> WHAT THE GERMANS lack is obviously my wish to be just to the Germans : I should not like to be unfaithful to myself in this matter , consequently I have to tell them what I ob jet to . <end>
<unchecked> <start> It costs dear to attain to power : power stupefied . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The Germans they were once called the nation of thinkers do they really at present think at all ? <end>

<unchecked> <start> In reality , it is something quite different which frightensBeer . <end>
<unchecked> <start> me German seriousness , German profundity , and Ger man passion in intellectual matters , are more and more on the decline . <end>

<unchecked> <start> I come in contact now and then with German universities : what an atmosphere prevails among their scholars , what withered , contented , and lukewarm in intellectuality ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> It would be a great misunderstanding if a person should adduce German science by way of objection to me , and , besides , it would be a proof that he had not read a word of my writings . <end>
<unchecked> <start> For seventeen years I have not tired of showing the in intellectually generating influence of our modern scientific pursuits . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The severe heroism to which the immense extent of the sciences at present condemns every in dividal , is a principal reason why the more fully , more richly , and more profoundly endowed natures no longer find suitable education and suitable educators . <end>
<unchecked> <start> There is nothing from which our civilisation suffers more than from the superfluity of presumptuous hod men and fragmental humanities our universities are , against their will , the real forcing houses for this mode of stunted growth of intellectual instincts . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And all Europe has already an idea of it grand politics deceive no body . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Germany is more and more regarded as the flat land of Europe . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I still seek for a German with whom might be serious in my own way , how much more for one with whom I could be cheerful ! <end>
