<unchecked> <start> who can conceive at present from Ji at seriousness a philosopher here recruits him self ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Our cheerfulness is what is least understood . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Let us make an estimate . <end>
<unchecked> <start> It is not only manifest that German civilisation declines , there is also sufficient reason for it . <end>
<unchecked> <start> No one can ultimately spend more than he possesses : that is true of individuals , it is true also of nations . <end>
<unchecked> <start> If we expend our means on power , grand politics , economy , international commerce , par , or military interests , if we give away the quantity of understanding , seriousness , will , and self overcoming , which constitutes us , on this side , it is lacking on the other . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Civilisation and the state let us not delude ourselves with regard to the antagonists : civilised state is merely a modern idea . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The one lives on the other , the one nourishes at the expense of the other . <end>
<unchecked> <start> All great periods of civilisation are periods of political decadence : whatever has been great as regards civilisation , has been non-political , even anti political . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Goethe s heart opened on the phenomenon of Napoleon , it closed on the War of Liberation . <end>
<unchecked> <start> At the same time that Germany comes forward as a great power , France acquires a changed importance as a power of civilisation . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Much new intellectual seriousness and passion is already transferred to Paris the question of pessimism , for example the question of Wagner , and almost all psychological and artistic questions are there discussed in an incomparably more refined and more thorough manner than in Germany , the Germans themselves are incapacitated for that kind of seriousness . <end>
<unchecked> <start> In the history of European civilisation there is one thing especially which the rise of the Empire indicates : a displacement of the centre of gravity . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Everybody is aware of it already : in the most important matter and that is civilisation the Germans are no longer of any account . <end>
<unchecked> <start> It is asked : have you even a single intellect to point to that counts in Europe , as your Goethe , your Hegel , your Heinrich Heine , and your Schopenhauer counted ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> There is no end of astonish ment that there is no longer a single German philo soper . <end>
<unchecked> <start> In all higher education in Germany , the main thing has been lost : the end , as well as the means for reaching it . <end>
<unchecked> <start> That education , culture , itself , is the end and not the Empire that for this end there is need of educators not public school teachers and university scholars : that has been forgotten . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Educators are necessary , who are themselves educated superior , noble intellects , who are proved every moment , who are proved whether they speak or are silent , mature and sweetened civilisations , not the learned lubbers which the public schools and universities at present offer to the youths as higher nurses . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The educators arc lacking save the exceptions of except tons the primary pre requisite of education : hence the decadence of German civilisation . <end>
<unchecked> <start> One of those rarest exceptions is my worthy friend , Jacob Burckhardt of Bale : it is to him , above all , that Bale owes its pre eminence in Humanity . <end>
<unchecked> <start> What the higher schools of Germany actually realise , is a brutal training in order that , with the least possible loss of time , an immense number of young men may be fitted to be used , used lp , as government officials . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Higher education and immense numbers that is a contradiction in principle . <end>
<unchecked> <start> All higher education belongs to the exceptions only : one has to be privileged to have a right to so high a privilege . <end>
<unchecked> <start> All that is great , all that is fine , can never be a common possession : fulcrum est homing . <end>
<unchecked> <start> What determines the decadence of German civilisation ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> That higher education is no longer a privilege democratise of universal , communist culture . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Not to forget that military privileges compel the too great attendance at the higher schools , which means their ruin . <end>
<unchecked> <start> In the Germany of to day no one is any longer at liberty to give his children a noble education : our higher schools are all of them adapted to the most equivocal mediocrity , as regards their teachers , plans of study , and educational aims . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And everywhere there is an unbecoming haste , as if something were wrong , when the young man of twenty three is not yet finished , does not yet know the answer to the main question : what calling ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> A higher class of men , let it be said , do not like callings , precisely because they know they are called . <end>
<unchecked> <start> They have time , they take their time , they do not at all think about getting finished at thirty years of age a person is a beginner , a child in the sphere of high civilisation . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Our over filled public-school , our overloaded , stupefied public school teachers are a scandal : there may perhaps be motives for de fending this condition of things , as the professors of Heidelberg have done recently , there are no reasons for it . <end>
<unchecked> <start> In order not to come short of my special mode which is affirmative , and only deals immediately and involuntarily with contradiction and criticism , I at once state the three tasks for the fulfilment of which educators are required . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The youth have to learn to see , they have to learn to think , they have to learn to speak and write : the object in all three cases is a noble civilisation . <end>
<unchecked> <start> To learn to see to accustom the eye to quietness , to patience , to reserve to postpone judgment , to survey and comprehend each case from all sides . <end>
<unchecked> <start> This is the first preliminary schooling for in intellectuality : not to react immediately upon a timu lus , but to get the checking , the settling instincts in hand . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Learning to see , as I understand it , is almost the same thing as in philosophical language is called strong will : the essential thing there is just not to will , the ability to defer decision . <end>
<unchecked> <start> All , all vulgarity rests on the inability to offer resistance to a stimulus people are obliged to react , they follow every impulse . <end>
<unchecked> <start> In many cases such a compulsion is already , decadence , a symptom of exhaustion , almost all that uphill optical crudeness designates by the word vice , is merely that physiological inability not to . <end>
<unchecked> <start> react . <end>
<unchecked> <start> A practical application of having learned to see : As learners , people will in general have become slow , mistrustful , and reluctant . <end>
<unchecked> <start> With hostile quietude they will let the strange and the new of every description approach at first , they will withdraw their hand , so as not to be touched by it . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The being open by all doors , the servile prostration before every insignificant fact , the continuous lurking to put one s self , to throw one s self among other people and other things , in short , vaunted modern objectivity is bad taste , it is ignoble par excellence . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Learning to think : people have no longer any notion of it in our schools . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Even in the universities , even among philosophical scholars themselves , logic begins to die out , alike as a theory , as a practice , and as a profession . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Let anyone read German books : there is no longer the remotest recollection that a technique , a plan of instruction , and a will to reach proficiency are required for thinking , that thinking requires to be learned as dancing requires to be learned , as a mode of dancing . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Who among the Germans as yet knows by experience that refined tremor which nimble feet in the field of intellect communicate to all muscles ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> The stiff of intellectual bearing , the clumsy hand in grasping that is German in such a degree that abroad it is altogether con founded with the German nature . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The German has no fingers for nuances . <end>
<unchecked> <start> That the Germans have even endured their philosophers , more especially that most deformed conceptual cripple that has ever existed , the great Kant , gives no small concept of German elegance . <end>
<unchecked> <start> In effect , no form of dancing can be ex clouded from a high class education ability to dance with the feet , with concepts , and with words : have I still to say one must be capable of it with the pen also one must learn to write ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> But at this point I should become a perfect puzzle to German readers . <end>

<unchecked> <start> moral for psychologists . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Never to occupy one s self with psychology ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Never to observe for the sake of observing ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> That results in false optics , in squinting , in something forced and exaggerated . <end>

<unchecked> <start> In experiencing anything , one mist not look towards one s self every look then becomes an evil eye . <end>
<unchecked> <start> A born psychologist is instinctively on his guard against seeing for the sake of seeing the same is true of the born painter . <end>
<unchecked> <start> He never works according to nature , he leaves the sifting and expressing of the case , of nature , or of the experienced , to his instinct , to his camera obscure . <end>
<unchecked> <start> He only becomes conscious of what is general , the conclusion , the result he is unacquainted with that arbitrary abstracting from single cases . <end>
<unchecked> <start> What is the result when people do otherwise ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> for example , when they carry on psychology after the manner of great and small Parisian romanciers ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> That mode of business lies in wait , as it were , for the actual , it brings home a handful of curiosities every even ing . <end>

<unchecked> <start> Nature , estimated artistically , is no model . <end>
<unchecked> <start> It exaggerates , it distorts , it leaves gaps . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Nature is accident . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Studying according to nature seems to me a bad sign it betrays subjection , weak ness , fatalism this lying in the dust before petits faith is unworthy of a complete artist . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Seeing what is that belongs to another species of intellects , to the anti artistic , to the practical . <end>
<unchecked> <start> One has to know who one is . <end>
<unchecked> <start> A psychology of the artist . <end>
<unchecked> <start> To the existence of art , to the existence of any aesthetic activity or perception whatsoever , a preliminary psychological condition is indispensable , namely , ecstasy . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Ecstasy must first have intensified the sensitiveness of the whole mechanism until this takes place art is not realised . <end>
<unchecked> <start> All kinds of ecstasy , however differently conditioned , possess this power above all the ecstasy of sexual excitement , the oldest and most primitive form of ecstasy . <end>
<unchecked> <start> In like manner the ecstasy which follows in the train of all great desires , of all strong emotions the ecstasy of the feast , of the contest , of a daring deed , of victory , of all extreme agitation the ecstasy of cruelty the ecstasy in destruction the ecstasy under certain meteorological influences for example , spring ecstasy or under the influence of narcotics finally , the ecstasy of will , the ecstasy of an overcharged and surging will . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The essential thing in ecstasy is the feeling of increased power and profusion . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Out of this feeling w T e impart to things , we constrain them to accept something from us , we force them by violence this proceeding is called realising . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Let us here free ourselves from a press dice : realising does not consist , as is commonly be lived , in an abstraction or deduction of the insignia cant or the contingent . <end>
<unchecked> <start> An immense forcing omit of principal traits is rather the decisive characteristic , so that the others thereby disappear . <end>
<unchecked> <start> In this condition we enrich everything out of our own profusion what we see , and what we wish for we see enlarged , crowded , strong , and overtaken with power . <end>

<unchecked> <start> What do the antithetical notions Apollinian and Dionysian which I have introduced into aesthetics imply , when we conceive of them both as modes of ecstasy ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Apollinian ecstasy above all keeps the eye on the alert , so that it acquires the faculty of vision . <end>

<unchecked> <start> In the Dionysian condition , on the other hand , the entire emotional system is excited , and has its energies augmented so that it discharges itself simultaneously by all channels of expression , and forces the faculties of representation , of imitation , of transfiguration , of metamorphosis all kinds of mimi cry and acting into activity at one and the same time . <end>

<unchecked> <start> If it were possible , a philo soper would be a nihilist , because he finds nothing ness behind all human ideals . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Or not even nothing ness , but only vileness , absurdity , sickness , cowardice , and fatigue : all sorts of dregs out of the drained goblet of his own life . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Man , who , as a reality , is so worthy of reverence , how is it that he deserves no respect in so far as he manifests his wishes ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Has he to do penance for being so accomplished as a reality ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Has he to compensate for his activity , for the exertion of thought and will in every activity , by the stretching of his limbs in the imaginary and absurd ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> The history of his has hitherto been the partie hortense of man one must be careful not to read too long in it . <end>
<unchecked> <start> What justifies man is his reality , it will for ever justify him . <end>
<unchecked> <start> How much more worthy is actual man , compared with any merely wished , dreamt , or shamelessly falsified man ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> compared with any ideal man whatsoever . <end>
<unchecked> <start> It is only ideal man that is distasteful to the philosopher . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Natural value of egotism . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Selfishness has as much value as the physiological value of him who possesses it : it may be very valuable , or it may be vile and contemptible . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Each individual may be looked at with respect to whether he represents an ascending or a descending line of life . <end>
<unchecked> <start> When that is deter mined , we have a canon for determining the value of his selfishness . <end>
<unchecked> <start> If he represent the ascent of the line of life , his value is in fact very great and on account of the collective life which in him makes a further step , the concern about his maintenance , about provide ing his optimum of conditions , may even be extreme . <end>
<unchecked> <start> For the single person , the individual , as hitherto understood both popularly and philosophically , is cer mainly an error : he is nothing by himself , no atom , no ring of the chain , nothing merely inherited from former times , he is the embodiment of the one entire line of descent up to himself . <end>
<unchecked> <start> If he represent des sending development , decay , chronic degeneration , or sickening diseases , taken on the whole , are phena mena which result from decay already present , they are not the causes of it , he has little worth , and the greatest fairness would have him take away as little as possible from the well constituted . <end>
<unchecked> <start> He is no more than their parasite then . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Christian and anarchist . <end>
<unchecked> <start> When the anarchist , as the mouth piece of degenerating strata of society , demands justice , righteousness and equal rights with embellished indignation , he is only under the influence of his lack of civilisation , which prevents him understanding why he is actually in trouble , in what respect he is impoverished , that it is in vital vigour that he is impoverished . <end>
<unchecked> <start> An impulse to seek for causes is strong in him : it must be somebody s fault that he is in a bad condition . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Even ember wished indignation itself is pleasant to him it is an enjoyment for every poor devil to vilify , it gives a taste of the ecstasy of power . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Even lamenting and bewailing one s self can give life a charm by which it becomes tolerable . <end>
<unchecked> <start> There is a refined dose of revenge in every lament people reproach those who are different from them for their own bad condition , and under certain circumstances even for their wicked ness , as if it were injustice , as if it involved permitted privilege . <end>
<unchecked> <start> If I be camille , thou shoulds be so also : it is on the basis of such logic that revolt tons arise . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Bewailing one s self never does any good : it originates from weakness . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Whether a person im puts his bad condition to others , or to himself the socialist does the former , and the Christian , for ex ample , does the latter it makes no essential difference . <end>
<unchecked> <start> That which both cases have in common , let us also say that which is unworthy in both cases , is that some body is to be blamed for the suffering in short , that the sufferer prescribes for himself the honey of revenge to alleviate his suffering . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The objects towards which this need of revenge , as a need of enjoyment , is directed are furnished by occasional causes the sufferer finds causes everywhere , which serve to cool his petty revenge , if he is a Christian , we repeat , he finds the causes in himself . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The Christian and the anarchist both are decadent . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But moreover , when the Christian condemns , calumnies and fouls the world , he does it from the same instinctive motive which impels the socialistic working man to condemn , and before society : doomsday even is the delicious com fort of revenge , revolution , the same as the socialistic working man expects , merely conceived as somewhat more remote . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The other world itself what would be the use of it , if it were not a means for fouling this world ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Criticism of decadence morality . <end>
<unchecked> <start> An altruistic morality , a morality which causes selfishness to lan guise , is , under all circumstances , a bad sign . <end>
<unchecked> <start> This is true of the individual , it is especially true of peoples . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The best is wanting , when selfishness begins to be de ancient . <end>
<unchecked> <start> To choose instinctively what is self injurious , to be alluded by disinterested motives , furnishes almost the formula for decadence . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Not to seek one s own advantage : that is merely the moral fig leaf for quite a different thing , for the physiological fact , one does not know any longer how to find one s own advantage . <end>
<unchecked> <start> disaggregation of instincts ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> It is at an end with him when man becomes altruistic . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Instead of naively saying , am no longer of any account , the moral falsehood in the mouth of the decadent says , nothing is of any account , life is of no account . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Such an opinion is ultimately a great danger it is con various , soon growing up luxuriantly to a tropical vegetation of ideas on the whole morbid soil of society , at one time as a religion Christianity , at another time as a philosophy schopenhauerian . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Under certain circumstances such ups tree vegetation , grown out of corruption , poisons life with its far reaching emanations for millenniums . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Morality for physicians . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The sick are parasites of society . <end>
<unchecked> <start> In certain conditions it is improper to live any longer . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The continued vegetation in cowardly dependence on physicians and prescriptions after demeaning of life , the right to life , has been lost , should entail the profound contempt of society . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The physicians , on the other hand , would have to be agents for com mutilating this contempt , not recipes for their patients , but every day a new dose of aversion from them . <end>
<unchecked> <start> To create a new responsibility , the physician s respond ability , for all cases where the highest interest of life , of ascending life , requires the remorseless crushing down and thrusting aside of degenerating life for example , for the right to procreation , for the right to be born , for the right to live . <end>
<unchecked> <start> To die proudly when it is no longer possible to live proudly Death selected voluntarily , death at the right time , consume mated with brightness and cheerfulness in the midst of children and witnesses : so that an actual leave taking is possible where he is yet present who takes his leave , as also an actual appraisement of what has been realised and aspired after , a summing up of life all in opposition to the pitiable and horrifying comedy which Christianity has practised with the hour of dying . <end>
<unchecked> <start> We must never forgive Christianity for having taken advantage of the weakness of the dying to outrage their consciences , for having misused even the mode of death to arrive at valuations of men and of the past Here , in spite of all cowardice of prejudice , it is primarily a question of re establishing the correct evaluation , t . <end>
<unchecked> <start> e . <end>
<unchecked> <start> physiological evaluation , of so called natural death , which , in the end , is nothing but an unnatural death , a suicide . <end>
<unchecked> <start> One is never destroyed by any one but one s self . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But natural death is a death under the most contemptible conditions , involuntary death , death at the wrong time , a coward s death . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Out of love of life we should desire a different kind of death voluntary , conscious , not accidental or by surprise . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Finally , an advice to Messrs , the pessimists and other decadent . <end>
<unchecked> <start> We have not it at our disposal to prevent being born we can , however , rectify this error for it is sometimes an error . <end>

<unchecked> <start> Pessimism itself does not make a single additional decadent I call to mind the result of the statistics , that the years in which the cholera rages do not differ from the other years in the total number of deaths . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Whether we are become more moral . <end>
<unchecked> <start> As was to be expected , the whole ferocity of moral stupefaction , which avowedly passes for morality itself in Germany , has taken up arms against my conception , beyond good and evil : I could tell fine stories about it . <end>
<unchecked> <start> My critics above all gave me the undeniable superiority of the moral sentiment of our age to reflect upon , the actual progress we have made in this respect in comparison with us , a Caesar Borgia was on no ac count to be set up in my fashion as a higher man , as a kind of beyond man . <end>
<unchecked> <start> A Swiss editor , of the Bund , went so far not without expressing his esteem of the courage for such a jeopardy as to understand the meaning of my work to the effect that I proposed to do away with all decent sentiment . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Very much obliged ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> I permit myself , as an answer , to raise the question , whether we are really become more moral . <end>
<unchecked> <start> That all the world believes it is already an objection against it . <end>
<unchecked> <start> We modern men , very delicate , very readily injured , giving and taking consideration in a hundred ways , we conceit ourselves in fact that this delicate humanity which we manifest , this realised unanimity in forbearance , in helpfulness , and in mutual trust is positive progress , and that we are thereby far above the men of the Renaissance . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Every age , however , thinks in this manner , it is obliged to think thus . <end>
<unchecked> <start> It is certain we could not place ourselves in Renaissance conditions we could not even conceive ourselves placed in them : our nerves would not stand that reality , not to speak of our muscles . <end>
<unchecked> <start> No progress , however , is demonstrated by this incapacity , but only a different , a later con edition , weaker , tendered , and more readily injured , out of which a considerate morality necessarily evolves . <end>
<unchecked> <start> If we were to think of our tenderness and lateness , our physiological aging , as absent , our womanising morality also would forthwith lose its value no mor laity has value in itself it would even let us despise it . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Let us not doubt , on the other hand , that we modern men , with our thick added humanity , which will not by any means strike against a stone , would furnish a comedy to the contemporaries of caesar Borgia to laugh themselves to death over . <end>
<unchecked> <start> In fact we are extraordinarily amusing , though involuntarily , with our modern virtues . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The decline of hostile and distrust awakening instincts for that would be our progress represents only one of the cone sequences in the general decline of vitality : it costs a hundred times more pains and more foresight to effectual an existence so conditioned and so late . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Under such circumstances people mutually assist one another to a certain extent everybody is sick , and everybody is a sick nurse . <end>
<unchecked> <start> That condition of things is then denominated virtue : among men who knew a different mode of life , fuller , more prodigal , more profuse , it would have had a different name , perhaps cowardice , , or old woman s morality . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Our softening of manners that is my thesis , it is , if you will , my innovation is a consequence of decadence severity , of manners may , inversely , be a consequence of super abundance of life : for then much can be dared , much can be challenged , and much also can be squandered . <end>
<unchecked> <start> What was formerly a seasoning of life would be poison to us . <end>
<unchecked> <start> To be indifferent that also is a form of strength for that likewise we are too old and too late : our morality of sympathy against which I w r as the first to give warning , that which one might designate as impressionism morale , is a further expression of the physiological over excitability possessed by all that is decadent . <end>
<unchecked> <start> That movement which has attempted to introduce itself scientifically by means of Schopenhauer s morality of sympathy a very unfortunate attempt ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> is the true decadence movement in morals , and , as such , is intrinsically related to Christian morality . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Vigorous eras , noble civilisations , see something contemptible in sympathy , in brotherly love , in the lack of self asset tion and self reliance . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Eras are to be measured by their positive powers : the period of the Renaissance accordingly , so profuse and fateful , presents itself as the last great period and we modern men , with our anxious self nursing and brotherly love , with our virtues of labour , pretentiousness , fair play , and scientific spirit accumulating , economic , mechanical , we re present a weak period . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Our virtues are determined , are peremptorily called forth by our weakness . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Equality , as an actual approximation to similarity , of which the theory of equal rights is but the ex expression , belongs essentially to decadence : the gap between man and man , between class and class , the multiplicity of types , the will to assert itself , to stand out in contrast , that which I call pathos of distance belongs to every vigorous period . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The power of stretch , the width of stretch between the extremes , becomes always smaller at present , the extremes themselves finally merge into similarity . <end>
<unchecked> <start> All our political theories and state constitutions , the German Empire by no means excepted , are consequences , resulting necessities , of decadence the unconscious operation of decadence has gained the ascendency so far as to affect the ideals of some of the sciences . <end>
<unchecked> <start> My objection against the whole of the sociology of England and France is that it only knows decaying types of society by ex experience , and quite innocently takes its own instincts of decay as the standard for sociological valuations . <end>

<unchecked> <start> separating , gap making , subordinating and power is formulated as the ideal , in the socio log of the present day . <end>

<unchecked> <start> Herbert Spencer , ho never , is also a decadent , he sees something desirable in the triumph of altruism . <end>
<unchecked> <start> My concept of freedom . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The worth of a thing lies sometimes not in what one attains with it , but in what one pays for it , what it costs us . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I give an ex ample . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Liberal institutions immediately cease to be liberal , so soon as they are attained afterwards , there are no more mischievous or more radical enemies of freedom than liberal institutions . <end>
<unchecked> <start> One knows well enough what they accomplish : they undermine the will to power , they are the levelling of mountain and valley exalted into morality , they make people small , cowardly , and voluptuous , with them the herding animal always triumphs . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Liberalism : that is in creased herding animality . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The same institutions produce quite other results so long as they are fought for they then , in fact , further freedom in a powerful manner . <end>
<unchecked> <start> On looking more accurately , we see that it is warfare which produces these results , warfare for liberal institutions , which , as war , allows illiberal in stints to continue . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And warfare educates for freedom . <end>
<unchecked> <start> For what is freedom ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> To have the will to be respond bible for one s self . <end>
<unchecked> <start> To keep the distance which separates us . <end>
<unchecked> <start> To become more indifferent to hardship , severity , privation , and even to life . <end>
<unchecked> <start> To be ready to sacrifice men for one s cause , one s self not excepted . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Freedom implies that manly instincts , instincts which delight in war and triumph , dominate over other instincts for example over the instincts of happiness . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The man who has become free , how much more the spirit which has become free , treads under foot the con species of well being dreamt of by shop keepers , Christians , cows , women , Englishmen , and other democrats . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The free man is a warrior . <end>
<unchecked> <start> How is freedom measured , in individuals , as well as in nations ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> By the resistance which has to be overcome , by the effort which it costs to retain superiority . <end>
<unchecked> <start> We should have to seek the highest type of free men where the highest resistance is constantly overcome : five paces from tyranny , close on the threshold of the danger of . <end>
<unchecked> <start> This is psychologically true , when we mean by tyrants pitiless and frightful instincts , which peremptorily call forth the maximum of authority and discipline the finest type is furnished by Julius Caesar it is also politically true let us but traverse the course of history . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The people who were worth something , who became worth something , never acquired their greatness under liberal institutions : great danger made something out of them which de serves reverence , danger which first teaches us to know our resources , our virtues , our shield and sword , our genius , which compels us to be strong . <end>
<unchecked> <start> First principle : men must require strength otherwise , they never attain it . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Those great forcing houses for the strong , the strongest species of man that has hitherto existed , the aristocratic commonwealth of the pattern of Rome and Venice , understood freedom precisely in the sense in which I understand the word : as something which one has and has not , as something which one desires , which one wins by conquest . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Criticism of modernism . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Our institutions are no longer worth anything : that is a matter on which we are unanimous . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But the fault is not in the institutions , but in us . <end>
<unchecked> <start> After we have lost all instincts out of which institutions grow , the institutions themselves are being lost , because we are no longer suitable for them . <end>
<unchecked> <start> democratise has always been the decadence type of organising power : I have already Human , All nonhuman , Vol . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Aphorism characterised modern de democracy together with its incomplete forms , such as the German Empire as a declining type of the state . <end>
<unchecked> <start> In order that there may be institutions , there must be a species of will , instinct , or imperative , even to salinity : a will for tradition , for au authority , for responsibility throughout centuries , a will for the solidarity of chains of generations forward and backward in infinite . <end>
<unchecked> <start> When this will exists , some thing establishes itself like the Imperium Romanum or like Russia , the only power at present which has durability in its constitution , which can wait , and can yet promise something , Russia , the antithetical con caption to the pitiable European petty state misery and nervousness , which has got into a critical condition with the establishment of the German Empire . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The entire western world no longer possesses those in stints out of which institutions grow , out of which futurity grows perhaps nothing is so much against the grain of its modern spirit . <end>
<unchecked> <start> We live for the present , we live very fast , we live very irresponsibly : this is precisely what we call freedom . <end>
<unchecked> <start> That which makes institutions in reality is despised , hated , and repudiated : wherever the word authority even be comes audible , people believe themselves in danger of a new slavery . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Decadence goes so far in the apple active instinct of our politicians and political parties , that they prefer instinctively what disintegrates , what hastens the end . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Witness modern marriage . <end>
<unchecked> <start> All rationality has evidently been lost in modern marriage that does not however furnish an objection against marriage , but against modernism . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Rationality of mar rage it lay in the sole legal responsibility of the husband : marriage thus possessed gravity , while at present it halts on both legs . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Rationality of mar rage it lay in its on principle : it thus acquired an emphasis which , opposed to the accident of sentiment , passion , and momentary impulse , knew how to make itself heard . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Rationality of mar rage it lay likewise in the responsibility of families for the selection of the spouses . <end>
<unchecked> <start> By the increasing indulgence in favour of marriages for love , the basis of marriage , that which first of all makes it an instil tuition , has been almost eliminated . <end>
<unchecked> <start> An institution is never , and never will be founded on an idiocy crash : marriage , as we have said , cannon be founded on love , it is founded on sexual impulse , on the impulse to possess property woman and child as property , on the impulse to rule , which constantly organises for itself the smallest type of sovereignty family , which needs children and heirs to maintain physiologically an acquired measure of power , influence and riches , to prepare for long tasks , and for from one century to another . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Marriage , as an institution , already involves the affirmation of the greatest and most permanent form of organisation : if society cannon as a whole pledge itself to the re modest generations , marriage has no meaning at all . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Modern marriage has lost its meaning , consequently , it is being done away with . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The labour question . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The fact that there is a labour question is owing to stupidity , or , at bottom , instinct degeneration , which is the cause of all existing stupidity . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Regarding certain things one does not question : the first imperative of instinct . <end>
<unchecked> <start> I do not at all understand what people want to do with the Euro mean working man , now that they have made a question of him . <end>
<unchecked> <start> He finds himself far too advantageously sitka ted not to go on questioning further , ever less mo deftly . <end>
<unchecked> <start> He has at last the majority on his side . <end>
<unchecked> <start> There is no hope now that a modest and self contented species of human being , a type like the Chinese , will here constitute itself into a class : this would have been the rational course , this would have been almost a necessity . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But what have people done ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> Everything possible to annihilate even the germ of the pre requisite for such a course through the most unjustifiable thoughtlessness people have fundamentally destroyed the instincts in virtue of which the working man becomes possible as a class , possible for himself . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The working man has been made capable of military ser vice , he has been given the right of combination and the right of the franchise : no wonder he already feels his existence as a state of exigency morally expressed , as injustice . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But what do people want ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> let it be asked once more . <end>
<unchecked> <start> If they want to realise an end , they must also be willing to use the means : if they want to have slaves , it is foolish to educate them to be masters . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Freedom w r which I do not mean . <end>
<unchecked> <start> In such times as the present , it is an additional peril to be left to one s instincts . <end>
<unchecked> <start> These instincts mutually contra diet , disturb , and destroy themselves I have already defined modernism as physiological self contradiction . <end>
<unchecked> <start> A rational education would claim that one , at least , of those instinct systems should be paralysed under an iron pressure , to enable another system to attain power , to become strong and predominant . <end>
<unchecked> <start> At pre sent one would have to make the individual possible in the first place , by pruning him . <end>
<unchecked> <start> To make him possible , that is to say , to make him an entirety . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The very reverse happens : independence , free dave moment , and aller are claimed the most vere gently precisely by those for whom no restraint would be too severe this is true in politics , it is true in art . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But that is a symptom of decadence : our modern notion of freedom is an additional proof of edge negation of instinct . <end>
<unchecked> <start> An allusion to Max von Schenkendorf s poem : freshest , die ich mine . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Where belief is necessary . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Nothing is rarer among moralists and saints than rectitude perhaps they say the contrary , perhaps they even believe it . <end>
<unchecked> <start> For when a belief is more useful , more efficacious , and more convincing than conscious hypocrisy , owing to instinct , hypocrisy forthwith becomes innocence : first prop position for understanding great saints . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Among philo hers also , another species of saints , the whole busi ness involves the necessity of only admitting certain truths , namely those on the basis of which their busi ness has public sanction , in Kantian language , the truths of practical reason . <end>
<unchecked> <start> They know what they must prove , they are practical therein , they recognise one another by being in mutual agreement with regard to truths . <end>

<unchecked> <start> e . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Mr . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Philosopher , be on your guard , lest you speak the truth . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Whispered into the ear of the conservatives . <end>
<unchecked> <start> What people did not know before , what they now know , or might know , a retrogression , a return in any sense , or to any extent , is quite impossible . <end>
<unchecked> <start> We physiologists , at least , know that . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But all priests and moralists have believed it possible , they wanted to bring mankind back , to screw mankind down to an of virtue . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Morality has always been a procrustean bed . <end>

<unchecked> <start> No one , however , is at liberty to be a crab . <end>

<unchecked> <start> We can check this development , and by checking it , we can dam up and collect edge negation itself , making it more vehement and sudden we cannon do more . <end>
<unchecked> <start> My notion of genius . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Great men , like great pe riots , are explosive materials in which an immense force is accumulated it is always pre requisite for such men , historically and physiologically , that for a long period there has been a collecting , a heaping up , an economising , and a hoarding , with respect to them , that for a long time no explosion has taken place . <end>
<unchecked> <start> When the tension in the substance has become too great , the most accidental stimulus suffices to call into the world the genius , the deed , and grand destiny . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Of what consequence then is the environs ment , the epoch , the spirit of the age , or public opinion ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Let us take the case of Napoleon . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The France of the Revolution and still more pre rev cautionary France would have produced a type anti chemical to Napoleon : it did produce it . <end>
<unchecked> <start> And because Napoleon was of a different type , the heir of a stronger , more enduring and older civilisation than that which vanished into vapour and fragments in France , he became master , he alone was the master here . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The great men are necessary , the time when they appear is contingent that they almost always become masters of their age , just depends on the fact that they are stronger , older , and possess longer acc mutated forces . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Between a genius and his age there exists a relation like that between the strong and the weak , between the old and the young : the age is , relatively , always much younger , more slender , more immature , more assured , and more childish . <end>

<unchecked> <start> Eternal life , eternal recurrence of life the future promised and consecrated in the past the triumphing affirmation of life beyond death and change true life , as the universal continuation of life by generation , by the mysteries of sexuality . <end>
<unchecked> <start> On that account , the sexual symbol was to the Greeks the symbol venerable in itself , the intrinsic profundity within all ancient piety . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Every detail in the act of generation , in pregnancy , and in birth , awakened the most exalted and solemn sentiments . <end>

<unchecked> <start> It is only Christianity , with its resentment against life at the bottom , which has caused sexuality to be regarded as something impure : it cast dirt on the commencement , on the pre requisite of our life . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The psychology of orgasm , as an exuberant feeling of life and energy , in which pain even operates as a stimulus , gave me the key to the concept of tragic feeling which has been misunderstood , as well by Aristotle , as especially by our pessimists . <end>

<unchecked> <start> The affirmation of life , even in its most unfamiliar and most severe problems , the will to live , enjoying its own in the sacrifice of its highest types , that is what I called Dionysian , that is what I divined as the bridge to a psychology of the tragic poet . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Not in order to get rid of terror and pity , not to purify from a dangerous passion by its vehement discharge it was thus that Aristotle understood it but , beyond terror and pity , to realise in fact the eternal delight of becoming , that delight which even involves in itself the joy of annihilating . <end>

<unchecked> <start> When the presuppositions of ascending life , when everything strong , brave , domineering , and proud have been eliminated out of the concept of God , when he sinks step by step to the symbol of a staff for the fat sued , a sheet anchor for all drowning ones , when he becomes the poor people s God , the sinners God , the God of the sick par excellence , and when the predicate of Saviour , Redeemer , is left as the sole divine predicate : what does such a change speak of ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> such a reduction of the divine ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> To be sure , the kingdom of God has thereby become greater . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Formerly , he had only his people , his chosen people . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Since then he has gone abroad on his travels , quite like his people itself , since then he has never again settled down quietly in any place : until he has finally become at home every where , the great cosmopolitan , till he has gained over the great number , and the half of earth to his side . <end>
<unchecked> <start> But the God of the great number , the democrat among Gods , became , nevertheless , no proud pagan God : he remained a Jew , he remained the God of the nooks , the God of all dark corners and places , of all unhealthy quarters throughout the world ! <end>

<unchecked> <start> The Christian concept of God God as God of the sick , God as cobweb spinner , God as spirit is one of the most corrupt concepts of God ever arrived at on earth it represents perhaps the gauge of low water in the descending development of the God type . <end>

<unchecked> <start> That the strong races of Northern Europe have not thrust from themselves the Christian God is verily no honour to their religious talent , not to speak of their taste . <end>
<unchecked> <start> They ought to have got the better of such a sickly and decrepit product of decadence . <end>
<unchecked> <start> There lies a curse upon them , because they have not got the better of it : they have incorporated sick ness , old age and contradiction into all their instincts , they have created no God since ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> Two millenniums almost , and not a single new God ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> But still continuing , and as if persisting by right , as an ultimatum and maximum of the God shaping force , of the creator spirits in man , this pitiable God of Christian monotony theism ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> This hybrid image of ruin , derived from nullity , concept and contradiction , in which all de cadence instincts , all cowardice and lassitude of soul have their sanction ! <end>
<unchecked> <start> With my condemnation of Christianity , I should not like to have done an injustice to a kindred religion , which even in the number of its followers , to Buddhism . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The two are related as nihilistic religions they are decadence religions , both are separated from one another in the most re remarkable manner . <end>

<unchecked> <start> Buddhism is the only properly positivist re legion which history sho vs us , even in its theory of perception a strict phenomenalism it no longer speaks of a struggle against sin , but , quite doing justice to actuality , it speaks of a struggle against suffering . <end>
<unchecked> <start> It has this distinguishes it profoundly from Christianity the self deception of moral concepts behind it it stands , in my language , beyond good and evil . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The two physiological facts on which it rests and which it has in view are , on the one hand , an ex massive of sensibility , which expresses itself as a refined capacity for pain , and , on the other hand , an over , an over long occupation with concepts and logical procedures through which the personal instinct has received damage to the ad vantage of the impersonal both are conditions , which at least some of my readers , the objective , will know , like myself , by experience . <end>
<unchecked> <start> On the basis of these physiological conditions a depression has originated : against which Buddha takes hygienic measures . <end>

<unchecked> <start> Buddhism is not a religion in which perfection is merely aspired after : the perfect is the normal case . <end>

<unchecked> <start> Buddhism is a religion for late men , for kind , gentle races who have become over intellectual and feel pain too readily Europe is as yet far from being ripe for it : it is a conveyance of them back to peace and cheer fullness , to regimen in intellectual matters , to a certain hardening in corporeal matters . <end>

<unchecked> <start> Buddhism , to repeat once more , is a hundred times colder , sincere and more objective . <end>

<unchecked> <start> Here the word devil was a : God send : people had an over powerful and terrible enemy , they did not need to be ashamed of suffering from such an enemy . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Christianity has some refinements at its basis which belong to the Orient . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Above all , Christianity knows that it is quite indifferent if aught is true , but of the highest importance so far as it is believed to be true . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Truth , and the belief that aught is true : two worlds with entirely exclusive interests , almost antithetical worlds , one arrives at each of the two by fund mentally different paths . <end>

<unchecked> <start> When however belief is necessary above everything else , reason , per caption , and investigation must be brought into discredit : the way to truth becomes a forbidden way . <end>

<unchecked> <start> On a soil , falsified to that extent where all natural ness , every natural value , all reality , had the profoundest instincts of the ruling class opposed to it , Christianity grew up , a form of mortal hostility to reality which has not hitherto been surpassed . <end>

<unchecked> <start> The case is of the first rank : the small seditious movement which is christened by the name of Jesus of Nazareth , is the Jewish instinct once more , expressed in other terms , the priestly instinct , which no longer endures the priest as a reality , the invention of a yet more abstract form of existence , a yet more unreal vision of the world , than is determined by the organisation of a church . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Christianity negatives the church . <end>

<unchecked> <start> Answer : Domineering Judaism , its upper class . <end>

<unchecked> <start> In every healthy society , three types , mutually conditioning and differently gravitating , physiologically separate themselves , each of which has its own hygiene , its own domain of labour , its own special sentiment of perfection , its own special mastership . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Nature , not Manu , separates from one another the mainly intellectual individuals , the in individuals mainly excelling in muscular strength , and the third class neither distinguished in the one nor in the other , the mediocre individuals , the latter as the great number , the former as the select individuals . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The highest caste I call them the fewest has , as the perfect caste , the privileges of the fewest : it belongs thereto to represent happiness , beauty , goodness on earth . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Only the most intellectual men have the permission to beauty , to the beautiful it is only with them that goodness is not weakness . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Pulchruni cst homing : the good is a privilege . <end>
<unchecked> <start> On the other hand , nothing can be less permissible to them than unpleasant manners or a pessimistic look , an eye that makes deformed , or even indignation with regard to the entire aspect of things . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Indignation is the privilege of the chantal and pessimism similarly . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The world is perfect thus speaks the instinct of the most intellectual men , affirmative instinct imperfection , every kind of in priority to us , distance , pathos of distance , even the chantal belong to this perfection . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The most intellectual men , as the strongest , find their happiness in that in which others would find their ruin : in the labyrinth , in severity towards themselves and others , in effort their delight is self overcoming : with them asceticism becomes naturalness , requirement , instinct . <end>
<unchecked> <start> A difficult task is regarded by them as a privilege , to play with burdens which crush others to death , as a recreation . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Knowledge , a form of asceticism . <end>
<unchecked> <start> They are the most venerable kind of man . <end>
<unchecked> <start> That does not exclude their being the most cheerful , the most amiable . <end>
<unchecked> <start> They rule , not because they will , but because they are they are not at liberty to be the second in rank . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The second in rank are : the guar diana of right , the keepers of order and security , the noble warriors , the king , above all , as the highest formula of warrior , judge , and keeper of the law . <end>
<unchecked> <start> The second in rank are the executive of the most in intellectual , the most closely associated with them , relief ing them of all that is coarse in the work of ruling , their retinue , their right hand , their best disciples . <end>
<unchecked> <start> In all that , to repeat it once more , there is nothing arbitrary , nothing artificial what is otherwise is artificial , by what is otherwise , nature is put to shame . <end>
<unchecked> <start> By the order of castes , the order of rank , the supreme law of life itself is formulated only the separation of the three types is necessary for the maintenance of society , for the making possible of higher and highest types , the inequality of rights is the very condition of there being rights at all . <end>
<unchecked> <start> A right is a privilege . <end>
<unchecked> <start> In his mode of existence every one has his privilege . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Let us not undervalue the privileges of the mediocre . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Life always becomes harder towards the summit , the cold increases , re responsibility increases . <end>
<unchecked> <start> A high civilisation is a pyramid : it can only stand upon a broad basis , it has for a first pre requisite a strongly and soundly consolidated mediocrity . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Handicraft , trade , agriculture , science , the greater part of art , in a word , the whole compass of business activity , is exclusively compatible with an average amount of ability and pretension the like pursuits would be displaced among the exceptions , the instinct appropriate thereto would contradict aristocratic as well as anarchism . <end>
<unchecked> <start> There is a determination of nature that a person should be a public utility , a wheel , a function : not society , the kind of happiness of which alone the larger number are capable , makes intelligent machines out of them . <end>
<unchecked> <start> For the mediocre , it is a happiness to be mediocre for them the mastery in one thing , specialism , is a natural instinct . <end>
<unchecked> <start> It would be altogether unworthy of a profounder intellect to see in mediocrity itself an objection . <end>
<unchecked> <start> It is indeed the first necessity for the possibility of exceptions : a high civilisation is conditioned by it . <end>
<unchecked> <start> If the exceptional man just treats the mediocre with a more delicate touch than himself and his equals , it is not mere cour test of heart , it is simply his duty . <end>
<unchecked> <start> Whom do I hate most among the mob of the present day ? <end>
<unchecked> <start> The Socialist mob , the chantal apostles , who undermine the working man s instinct , his pleasure , his feeling of connectedness with his petty existence , who make him envious , who teach him revenge . <end>

<unchecked> <start> If we just became acquainted with a religious legislation whose object was to make eternal the highest condition for making life flourish , a great organisation of society , Christianity , on the other hand , found its mission in putting an end to just such an organisation , because life flourished in it . <end>
<unchecked> <start> There the proceeds of reason from long periods of experiment and uncertainty were intended to be invested for the most remote advantage and the harvest was intended to be brought home as large , as rich , and as complete as possible : here , reverse , the harvest was blighted during the night . <end>
